<p>Your lab partner is trying again (eye roll) and did another a chi-squared (&chi;<sup>2</sup>) test on the F<sub>2</sub> generation in a dihybid cross based on your lab data (above). They wanted to know if the results confirm the expected phenotype ratios.</p><p>You helped them set up the null hypothesis, so you know that part is correct, but they got confused and were unsure about how to calculate the chi-squared (&chi;<sup>2</sup>) value. So much so that they did it three (3) different ways.</p> <p>Before you ask your instructor for a new lab partner, <b>tell them which table is correct AND whether they can accept or reject the null hypothesis</b> using the information provided.</p> 	table 1 is correct and we <b>reject</b> the null hypothesis	Incorrect	table 2 is correct and we <b>reject</b> the null hypothesis	Incorrect	table 3 is correct and we <b>reject</b> the null hypothesis	Incorrect	table 1 is correct and we <b>accept</b> the null hypothesis	Incorrect	table 2 is correct and we <b>accept</b> the null hypothesis	Correct	table 3 is correct and we <b>accept</b> the null hypothesis	Incorrect

<p>Your lab partner is trying again (eye roll) and did another a chi-squared (&chi;<sup>2</sup>) test on the F<sub>2</sub> generation in a dihybid cross based on your lab data (above). They wanted to know if the results confirm the expected phenotype ratios.</p><p>You helped them set up the null hypothesis, so you know that part is correct, but they got confused and were unsure about how to calculate the chi-squared (&chi;<sup>2</sup>) value.
